<analysis>**original_problem_statement:**
The user wants to add a new feature related to customer reservations. If a customer's reservation is deleted (either automatically due to expiration or manually by an admin), and that same customer generates a new sale (omset) for their *previous* owner, the system should automatically re-establish the reservation for that customer under that staff member, provided the customer is not currently reserved by someone else.

**User's preferred language**: English

**what currently exists?**
The application is a full-stack CRM with a React frontend and a Python/Flask/MongoDB backend. In this session, numerous features and critical bug fixes were implemented. Key additions include: a fine system for  (permit) overages, a daily briefing modal for staff, configurable staff working hours, and per-database controls for auto-approving record requests. Several critical bugs were also resolved, including a widespread authentication failure on all file exports and a recurring logic bug in the new per-database auto-approve feature. The agent also performed a comprehensive code quality cleanup, resolving all linting issues in the backend routes at the user's request.

**Last working item**:
- **Last item agent was working:** The agent was beginning to implement the user's latest feature request: automatically re-assigning an expired/deleted reserved member to their previous owner if that owner records a new omset from them. The agent had started its investigation by examining the omset recording logic in .
- **Status:** IN PROGRESS
- **Agent Testing Done:** N
- **Which testing method agent to use?** backend testing agent
- **User Testing Done:** N

**All Pending/In progress Issue list**:
- There are no pending issues. The current work is a new feature implementation, which is tracked in the Task List.

**In progress Task List**:
- **Task 1: (P0) Implement Auto-Reassignment of Expired Reserved Members on New Omset**
  - **Where to resume**: The investigation has started in . The next step is to modify the  endpoint logic. The implementation should:
    1.  When an omset is recorded, check if the customer has a recently deleted reservation record (e.g., in a separate log or by checking for an inactive reservation).
    2.  Verify the customer is not currently reserved by any other staff member.
    3.  If both conditions are met, create a new  entry for the customer, assigning them to the staff member who recorded the omset.
  - **What will be achieved with this?**: This automates the process of reclaiming valuable customers for staff who maintain relationships after a formal reservation lapses, improving staff retention of key clients.
  - **Status:** IN PROGRESS
  - **Should Test frontend/backend/both after fix?**: backend
  - **Blocked on something:** None

**Upcoming and Future Tasks**
**Upcoming Tasks:**
-   **P1: UI/UX consistency standardization**: Standardize UI elements like buttons, modals, colors, and table formats across the application.

**Future Tasks:**
-   **P2: Smart Message Queue App**: A separate application for WhatsApp follow-ups.
-   **P2: Staging/testing environment setup**: Set up a separate staging environment for thorough testing.
-   **P2: Centralized logging & monitoring**: Integrate a service like Sentry or LogRocket (the user has de-prioritized this for now).

**Completed work in this session**
- **Critical Bug Fix: Per-Database Auto-Approve Logic (RESOLVED)**: Fixed a recurring bug where the Manual approval setting was ignored. The root causes (a Pydantic model stripping the API response field and a faulty boolean check) were identified and fixed. The entire feature was verified with a comprehensive testing agent run.
- **Feature: Configurable Staff Working Hours**: Implemented a UI for admins to set custom staff start/end times, replacing hardcoded values used in lateness calculations.
- **Critical Bug Fix: Global Export Authentication Failure (RESOLVED)**: Fixed an app-wide bug where all file exports failed due to authentication issues. The fix involved adding a token-based query parameter authentication fallback to all export endpoints.
- **Feature: Per-Database Auto-Approve Toggle**: Implemented UI and backend logic for admins to set approval rules (Auto/Manual) for each database individually, overriding the global setting.
- **Feature: Randomized Record Assignment**: Changed the record assignment logic for the normal database from sequential to random to prevent staff from receiving duplicate customers.
- **Feature: Daily Staff Briefing Modal**: Created a daily pop-up modal for staff showing a random selection of their at-risk customers and follow-up reminders.
- **Feature: Izin Overage Fee System & Manual Deletion**: Implemented a fee for  (permit) time taken over the daily limit and added a feature for admins to manually waive these fees.
- **Bug Fix: At-Risk Telegram Alert Logic**: Corrected the Telegram alert to exclude lost customers (inactive >30 days).
- **Improvement: Secondary Phone Number Support**: Updated UI components to correctly format and add functionality (copy button, WhatsApp link) to a secondary phone number column in data tables.
- **Code Quality: Full Backend Linting**: Addressed user feedback by performing a full linting pass on all backend route files, fixing 15+ pre-existing issues.

**Earlier issues found/mentioned but not fixed**
-   None. All issues raised by the user in this session were addressed.

**Known issue recurrence from previous fork**
-   **Issue recurrence in this fork**: The Per-Database Auto-Approve feature was delivered broken and required two separate fixes. The first fix addressed the UI not updating, and the second fixed the core logic where Manual requests were still being auto-approved.
-   **Recurrence count**: 2
-   **Status**: RESOLVED. This highlights the need for rigorous end-to-end testing before marking a feature as complete.

**Key Technical Concepts**
-   **Backend**: Python, Flask, MongoDB ()

-   **Authentication**: A dual-auth pattern is now established:  header for standard API calls and  query parameter for file downloads initiated via  or iframes. A helper for this exists in .
-   **Pydantic Model Validation**: A key lesson was that Pydantic s will silently strip any fields from an API response that are not explicitly defined in the model. This was the root cause of the auto-approve UI bug.

**Critical Info for New Agent**
-   **User Trust is Fragile**: The user became extremely frustrated when the auto-approve feature was delivered broken twice. They explicitly called out the agent's carelessness. You MUST be extremely thorough in your testing. Verify the full end-to-end flow (backend logic, API response, UI display, and user interaction) before marking anything as complete.
-   **The Pydantic Model Bug**: Be aware that if you add a field to a MongoDB collection and expect it in an API response, you MUST also add that field to the Pydantic  in the route. Otherwise, it will be silently filtered out.
